# Skyrim:Dungeons

## Overview

A typical dungeon

This page provides general information on what to expect when exploring **dungeons**. Here, "dungeon" is being used as a general term to refer to the underground sections of all the various [places](/wiki/Skyrim:Places "Skyrim:Places") in the game: e.g., [caves](/wiki/Skyrim:Caves "Skyrim:Caves"), [Dwarven ruins](/wiki/Skyrim:Dwarven_Ruins "Skyrim:Dwarven Ruins"), [mines](/wiki/Skyrim:Mines "Skyrim:Mines"), [Nordic ruins](/wiki/Skyrim:Nordic_Ruins "Skyrim:Nordic Ruins"), etc. Some of the information is also relevant to above-ground areas, at the entrance to a dungeon or in various locations containing enemies that are entirely above-ground.

## Radiant System

As part of Skyrim's [Radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant") system, most dungeons have the potential to host a range of randomly-assigned quests. Some quests will be assigned to any type of dungeon; other quests are only assigned to dungeons containing a specific type of enemy (e.g., bandits or undead).

These randomly-assigned quests take advantage of certain predefined points within each dungeon. In particular:

- Boss: the final and most difficult enemy in the dungeon. Some quests will replace the boss with a quest-specific enemy (although this feature often causes bugs).
- Boss Chest: each dungeon has one container that is tagged as that dungeon's boss chest. Any items that need to be retrieved for a quest will be found in the boss chest. (Note that some dungeons have other types of containers labeled as their boss container, such as knapsacks or even egg sacs.)
- Captive Marker: the location where any quest-related captives (e.g., kidnapped citizens) are put. Typically some type of cell.

One implication of this system is that if multiple quests are assigned to the same dungeon, all of the quest-related items are put in the same place: multiple captives will be locked in same cell, or multiple quest items will be found in the same chest.

## Levels

Many dungeons in Skyrim have a defined minimum level; some also have a maximum level. These levels do *not* determine whether or not your character can enter the dungeon. Rather, they determine the difficulty of the enemies located in the dungeon and the quality of the loot that will be found.[*verification needed — Need in-game confirmation that both enemies and loot are controlled by dungeon level*] Normally, all enemies and loot are generated based on your character's current level. However, if your level is lower than the dungeon's minimum level, the enemies and loot are instead generated using that minimum level — resulting in enemies that are more difficult to kill, but also higher-quality loot.

## Clearing

Most dungeons are "clearable", meaning that once the boss is defeated, the dungeon is tagged as "Cleared". A (somewhat quiet) tone will play once this occurs. A cleared dungeon may still have unkilled enemies and uncollected loot. This status is shown on the in-game map, allowing you to identify which dungeons you have or have not visited. If a dungeon has been cleared, it will take longer for its contents to [respawn](#Respawning). Its status remains as "Cleared" even if the occupants have all respawned.

There are a total of 197 [places](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Clearable "Category:Skyrim-Places-Clearable") in the game that can be cleared, although two of them ([Angarvunde](/wiki/Skyrim:Angarvunde "Skyrim:Angarvunde") and [Mistwatch](/wiki/Skyrim:Mistwatch "Skyrim:Mistwatch")) are atypical, as detailed in the next paragraph. Once you have cleared any 50 of the remaining 195 locations, the [Delver](/wiki/Skyrim:Delver "Skyrim:Delver") achievement is unlocked. However, a significant number of dungeons cannot be cleared at all; the wiki page for each of these dungeons states "Clearable: No" on the page's infobox.

Angarvunde and Mistwatch are the only locations in the game that are marked as cleared when a related quest is completed, instead of when the location's boss enemy is killed. The specific requirements necessary to clear these locations are detailed on their place pages. One consequence of being marked as cleared by a quest is that these two locations do *not* increment the Dungeons Cleared statistic or count towards the Delver achievement. In several other cases (detailed in the [Achievements](#Achievements) section), a "Cleared" tag appears when a nearby location has been cleared.

If a "Cleared" location is capable of respawning, it may be visited and looted again but its "Cleared" tag always remains as "Cleared". There is no way to tell from the map alone whether such a "Cleared" location has undergone a respawn.

**Note**: a clearable location target of [Kill the Bandit Leader](/wiki/Skyrim:Kill_the_Bandit_Leader "Skyrim:Kill the Bandit Leader") ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant")) quest will get the "Cleared" tag when you report back to the Quest Giver, not when the boss is defeated.

## Respawning

When a dungeon respawns, its enemies and loot are reset.

*Main article: [Respawning](/wiki/Skyrim:Respawning "Skyrim:Respawning")*

## Occupants

Skyrim's dungeons are categorized according to their occupants, and fall into one of these categories:

- [Animal Den](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Animal_Dens "Category:Skyrim-Places-Animal Dens") (9 out of 13 *whose minimum level is given on their wiki page* are minimum level 2)
- [Bandit Camp](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Bandit_Camps "Category:Skyrim-Places-Bandit Camps") (20 out of 21 are minimum level 6)
- [Dragon Lair](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Dragon_Lairs "Category:Skyrim-Places-Dragon Lairs")
- [Dragon Priest Lair](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Dragon_Priest_Lairs "Category:Skyrim-Places-Dragon Priest Lairs") (6 out of 6 are minimum level 24)
- [Draugr Crypt](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Draugr_Crypts "Category:Skyrim-Places-Draugr Crypts") (18 out of 20 are minimum level 6)
- [Dwarven Automaton Site](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Dwarven_Automaton_Sites "Category:Skyrim-Places-Dwarven Automaton Sites") (6 out of 7 are minimum level 16)
- [Falmer Hive](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Falmer_Hives "Category:Skyrim-Places-Falmer Hives") (16 out of 17 are minimum level 18)
- [Forsworn Camp](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Forsworn_Camps "Category:Skyrim-Places-Forsworn Camps") (6 out of 6 are minimum level 14)
- [Giant Camp](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Giant_Camps "Category:Skyrim-Places-Giant Camps") ([Sleeping Tree Camp](/wiki/Skyrim:Sleeping_Tree_Camp "Skyrim:Sleeping Tree Camp") is minimum level 2, [Guldun Rock](/wiki/Skyrim:Guldun_Rock "Skyrim:Guldun Rock") is minimum level 24)
- [Hagraven Nest](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Hagraven_Nests "Category:Skyrim-Places-Hagraven Nests") (5 out of 5 are minimum level 14)
- [Spriggan Grove](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Spriggan_Groves "Category:Skyrim-Places-Spriggan Groves") ([Shrouded Grove](/wiki/Skyrim:Shrouded_Grove "Skyrim:Shrouded Grove") is minimum level 8)
- [Vampire Lair](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Vampire_Lairs "Category:Skyrim-Places-Vampire Lairs") (7 out of 7 are minimum level 6)
- [Warlock Lair](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Warlock_Lairs "Category:Skyrim-Places-Warlock Lairs") (10 out of 16 are minimum level 8)
- [Werewolf Lair](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Werewolf_Lairs "Category:Skyrim-Places-Werewolf Lairs") ([Rimerock Burrow](/wiki/Skyrim:Rimerock_Burrow "Skyrim:Rimerock Burrow") is minimum level 6)

The specific occupants that you encounter in any dungeon are for the most part randomly generated and level-dependent. Most dungeon categories seem to have a preferred minimum level which applies to most of the dungeons in a category. See [levels](#Levels) for information on the level used to generate the occupants. Most enemies are named based on their level. For example, a low-level Necromancer is named "Novice Necromancer", whereas the top-level Necromancers are named "Arch Necromancer".

## Loot

Most of the loot found in a dungeon is randomly generated based upon your character's level and/or the dungeon's level (see [levels](#Levels)). The amount of gold you will find is level-dependent, as is the quality of the items that you will find. [Item](/wiki/Skyrim:Items "Skyrim:Items")-related articles such as [Armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Armor "Skyrim:Armor"), [Weapons](/wiki/Skyrim:Weapons "Skyrim:Weapons"), [Generic Magic Apparel](/wiki/Skyrim:Generic_Magic_Apparel "Skyrim:Generic Magic Apparel"), and [Generic Magic Weapons](/wiki/Skyrim:Generic_Magic_Weapons "Skyrim:Generic Magic Weapons") provide details on the level at which various items can be found.

Level-dependent items include:

- Contents of most [chests and other loot containers](/wiki/Skyrim:Containers "Skyrim:Containers")
- Some items sitting out in the open. Unlike previous Elder Scrolls games, in Skyrim developers can place [dummy objects](/wiki/Skyrim:Template_Items#Dummy_Items "Skyrim:Template Items"), for example on tables or shelves. These dummy objects are then replaced by a leveled item when the dungeon contents are spawned. This is most frequently done with potions, but is also done for armor, arrows, books, soul gems, and weapons.

### Special Loot

Some of the loot found in chests is designated as "special loot", these items are generated using a modified level. Special loot gives a chance at higher-quality items, up to what would normally be possible only for a character twice your level minus one[*verification needed*]. Armor, weapons, and spell tomes can be generated as special loot. Locations where special loot can be found include:

- Every boss chest is guaranteed to contain one special loot item.
- Most standard dungeon chests have a 10% chance of containing one special loot item.
  - The [Lockpicking](/wiki/Skyrim:Lockpicking "Skyrim:Lockpicking") perk Treasure Hunter increases this chance to 15%.

## Achievements

[Achievements](/wiki/Skyrim:Achievements "Skyrim:Achievements") related to dungeons include:

-  **Delver** (40 points/Silver) — Clear 50 dungeons
  - To obtain this achievement, you need to not only discover 50 dungeons, but also [clear](#Clearing) each location by killing its boss. The number of locations that you have cleared can be tracked using the "Dungeons Cleared" statistic in your journal. 197 locations can be cleared, all of which are listed in the [clearable category](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Clearable "Category:Skyrim-Places-Clearable"). However:
    - Two of the clearable locations, [Angarvunde](/wiki/Skyrim:Angarvunde "Skyrim:Angarvunde") and [Mistwatch](/wiki/Skyrim:Mistwatch "Skyrim:Mistwatch"), display as cleared on your map but do not increment the Dungeons Cleared statistic or count towards the Delver achievement.
    - Several other locations that may show up as "Cleared" on your map are actually secondary locations — the "Cleared" tag appears when the associated primary location is cleared. None of these secondary locations count towards the Dungeon Cleared statistics or count towards the achievement, and are not shown in the Cleared category, or counted in the above total of 186 clearable locations. These places include [Giant's Grove](/wiki/Skyrim:Giant%27s_Grove "Skyrim:Giant's Grove"), [Klimmek's House](/wiki/Skyrim:Klimmek%27s_House "Skyrim:Klimmek's House"), [Shalidor's Maze](/wiki/Skyrim:Shalidor%27s_Maze "Skyrim:Shalidor's Maze"), and [Sundered Towers](/wiki/Skyrim:Sundered_Towers "Skyrim:Sundered Towers").
    - Some locations have two map markers and therefore count twice towards the [Explorer](/wiki/Skyrim:Explorer "Skyrim:Explorer") achievement (and cause "Cleared" to display two times on your in-game map), but still only count once towards the "Dungeons Cleared" statistic. These places include North/South [Brittleshin Pass](/wiki/Skyrim:Brittleshin_Pass "Skyrim:Brittleshin Pass"), North/South [Cold Rock Pass](/wiki/Skyrim:Cold_Rock_Pass "Skyrim:Cold Rock Pass"), North/South [Shriekwind Bastion](/wiki/Skyrim:Shriekwind_Bastion "Skyrim:Shriekwind Bastion"), North/South [Skybound Watch Pass](/wiki/Skyrim:Skybound_Watch_Pass "Skyrim:Skybound Watch Pass"), [Steepfall Burrow](/wiki/Skyrim:Steepfall_Burrow "Skyrim:Steepfall Burrow") with its lower entrance, and [Reachcliff Cave](/wiki/Skyrim:Reachcliff_Cave "Skyrim:Reachcliff Cave") with its secret entrance.
    - [Official Add-Ons](/wiki/Skyrim:Add-ons "Skyrim:Add-ons") and some mods may change the total number of clearable locations.

Dunmer Ghost

Three **Dunmer Ghosts** can be found when retrieving the Crown Of Barenziah in [Tolvald's Cave](/wiki/Skyrim:Tolvald%27s_Cave "Skyrim:Tolvald's Cave") after finding all 24 [Unusual Gems](/wiki/Skyrim:Unusual_Gem "Skyrim:Unusual Gem") (Stones of Barenziah) during the quest [No Stone Unturned](/wiki/Skyrim:No_Stone_Unturned "Skyrim:No Stone Unturned"). They are the [ghosts](/wiki/Skyrim:Ghost "Skyrim:Ghost") of the ambushed [Dunmer](/wiki/Skyrim:Dark_Elf "Skyrim:Dark Elf") caravan of refugees from [Morrowind](/wiki/Lore:Morrowind "Lore:Morrowind").
One of the ghosts appears to be sitting next to her skeleton and was a battle mage prior to being in the caravan as can be learned from the journal where she is sitting. This ghost will at times respond to spells equipped if you have them "unsheathed". The second appears to be wearing full elven armor but does not appear to have any dialogue options. The third ghost is located to the right of the Crown of Barenziah beside a pillar.

## Related Quests

- **[No Stone Unturned](/wiki/Skyrim:No_Stone_Unturned "Skyrim:No Stone Unturned")**: Find the [24 gems](/wiki/Skyrim:Unusual_Gem "Skyrim:Unusual Gem") to restore the Crown of Barenziah.

# Skyrim:Dunmeth Pass

## Overview

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| |  | | --- | | Landmark: Dunmeth Pass ([view on map](https://gamemap.uesp.net/sr/?world=Skyrim&centeron=Dunmeth+Pass)) ([lore page](/wiki/Lore:Dunmeth_Pass "Lore:Dunmeth Pass")) | | |
| [Respawn Time](/wiki/Skyrim:Respawn "Skyrim:Respawn") | 10 days |
| Region | |
| [Eastmarch](/wiki/Skyrim:Eastmarch "Skyrim:Eastmarch") | |
| Location | |
| East of [Windhelm](/wiki/Skyrim:Windhelm "Skyrim:Windhelm") | |

View of Dunmeth Pass looking west

**Dunmeth Pass** is a mountain [pass](/wiki/Skyrim:Border_Gates "Skyrim:Border Gates") and one of the few traversable roads through the [Velothi Mountains](/wiki/Lore:Velothi_Mountains "Lore:Velothi Mountains") between northwest [Morrowind](/wiki/Lore:Morrowind "Lore:Morrowind") and northeast [Skyrim](/wiki/Lore:Skyrim "Lore:Skyrim").

On the Morrowind side, the pass is near the city of [Blacklight](/wiki/Lore:Blacklight "Lore:Blacklight"), and in Skyrim, it emerges near the city of [Windhelm](/wiki/Skyrim:Windhelm "Skyrim:Windhelm"). It historically served as a significant avenue of trade for Windhelm, although traffic has likely diminished since the [Red Year](/wiki/Lore:Red_Year "Lore:Red Year").

At the conclusion of [Find the Thalmor Assassin](/wiki/Skyrim:Find_the_Thalmor_Assassin "Skyrim:Find the Thalmor Assassin"), [Malborn](/wiki/Skyrim:Malborn "Skyrim:Malborn") exits [New Gnisis Cornerclub](/wiki/Skyrim:New_Gnisis_Cornerclub "Skyrim:New Gnisis Cornerclub"), and runs all the way to the Morrowind border at [Refugees' Rest](/wiki/Skyrim:Refugees%27_Rest "Skyrim:Refugees' Rest"), where he will disappear from the game.

## Related Quests

- **[Find the Thalmor Assassin](/wiki/Skyrim:Find_the_Thalmor_Assassin "Skyrim:Find the Thalmor Assassin")**: The [Thalmor](/wiki/Skyrim:Thalmor "Skyrim:Thalmor") are after [Malborn](/wiki/Skyrim:Malborn "Skyrim:Malborn"). Help him get to safety.

Durak

**Durak** is an [Orc](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc "Skyrim:Orc") [ranger](/wiki/Skyrim:Ranger_(class) "Skyrim:Ranger (class)") and a [vampire](/wiki/Skyrim:Vampire "Skyrim:Vampire") hunter. He is the first to approach you about the recent vampire menace and recruits you into the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_(faction) "Skyrim:Dawnguard (faction)"). If you speak with him in [Dayspring Canyon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dayspring_Canyon "Skyrim:Dayspring Canyon"), he will give you a [crossbow](/wiki/Skyrim:Crossbow "Skyrim:Crossbow") and 45 [steel bolts](/wiki/Skyrim:Steel_Bolt "Skyrim:Steel Bolt"). He will tell you that the crossbow is a "Dawnguard specialty" and is the best weapon to use when trying to take down vampires.

Durak will be available as a follower once the quest [Prophet](/wiki/Skyrim:Prophet_(Dawnguard) "Skyrim:Prophet (Dawnguard)") is completed. Completing said quest will also cause him to make you [Blood-Kin](/wiki/Skyrim:Blood-Kin "Skyrim:Blood-Kin"), granting you access to all [Orc Strongholds](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc_Strongholds "Skyrim:Orc Strongholds"). He is also one of the few followers who has no maximum level, meaning he will continue to level up with you.

He wears a set of [Dawnguard armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_Armor "Skyrim:Dawnguard Armor"), including matching pairs of [gauntlets](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_Gauntlets "Skyrim:Dawnguard Gauntlets") and [boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_Boots "Skyrim:Dawnguard Boots"). He is equipped with a [Dawnguard war axe](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_War_Axe "Skyrim:Dawnguard War Axe") and a [Dawnguard shield](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_Shield "Skyrim:Dawnguard Shield"). He will switch to a [crossbow](/wiki/Skyrim:Crossbow "Skyrim:Crossbow") supplemented with 14 [steel bolts](/wiki/Skyrim:Steel_Bolt "Skyrim:Steel Bolt") for long range attacks should the need arise.

## Related Quests

- **[Find out about the Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Find_out_about_the_Dawnguard "Skyrim:Find out about the Dawnguard")**: Speak with the leader of the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_(faction) "Skyrim:Dawnguard (faction)").
- **[Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_(quest) "Skyrim:Dawnguard (quest)")**: Speak with the leader of the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_(faction) "Skyrim:Dawnguard (faction)").
- **[Destroying the Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Destroying_the_Dawnguard "Skyrim:Destroying the Dawnguard")**: Kill the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_(faction) "Skyrim:Dawnguard (faction)") leaders.
- **[Kindred Judgment](/wiki/Skyrim:Kindred_Judgment "Skyrim:Kindred Judgment")**: Confront [Lord Harkon](/wiki/Skyrim:Lord_Harkon "Skyrim:Lord Harkon").

### Dawnguard

He will approach you in one of the major cities, or you can talk to him in Dayspring Canyon:

:   *"You there. The Dawnguard is looking for anyone willing to fight against the growing vampire menace. What do you say?"*

:   :   **What's the Dawnguard?**
    :   *"We're vampire hunters. We search out and destroy those bloodsucking scum wherever we find them."*

:   :   **Sorry, I'm not interested.**
    :   *"That's what everybody says, right up until they find their throat being ripped out by a pack of hungry vampires."*

:   :   **I haven't noticed any vampire menace.**
    :   *"You're not paying attention then. Like most everyone else around here. Haven't you heard that the Hall of the Vigilants was destroyed by vampires? They never took the threat seriously, and now they've paid the price."*

        :   **Vigilants? Dawnguard? What are you talking about?**
        :   *"The Vigilants mostly hunt down daedra worshippers, which is why they got torn to pieces when they went up against vampires. That's why our leader Isran is reestablishing the Dawnguard. Real, serious vampire hunters."*

:   :   **Killing vampires? Where do I sign up?**
    :   *"Ha. Isran's going to like you. Go talk to him at Fort Dawnguard, southeast of Riften. He'll decide if you're Dawnguard material."*

If you ask him this question in Dayspring Canyon:

:   :   *"Ha. Isran's going to like you. He's up the hill, in the fort. He'll decide if you're Dawnguard material."*

If spoken to again if you've said you weren't interested he can say:

:   *"Changed your mind, huh? The Dawnguard could use somebody like you."*
:   *"Yeah? You change your mind? The Dawnguard could use somebody like you."*

If spoke to again if you offered to join up:

:   *"Report to Isran at Fort Dawnguard. And get moving if you're serious about it. The vampires aren't going to wait around to make their next move."*

When spoken to at Fort Dawnguard:

:   *"Well, well. You made it. Good. Isran's in the fort. He'll get you sorted out."*
:   *"Glad you decided to give it a try. I hope Isran likes you."*
:   *"If you're here to join up, you need to see Isran. He's up at the fort talking to some Vigilant."*

:   :   **What's that you're shooting with?**
    :   *"Never seen a crossbow before, eh? Not surprised. Kind of a Dawnguard specialty. Nothing better for putting down vampires. Here, take this one and give it a try. You'll want to get to know how to use it if you really plan to join the Dawnguard."*

If you ask him this question again, he mentions the crossbow again, but stops speaking after explaining that crossbows are excellent for eliminating vampires and won't give you another one.

### Kindred Judgment

During Isran's speech he will say:

:   *"The prophecy is no more!"*

During this quest he can shout:

:   *"It is time for action."*
:   *"Destroy every last one of them!"*

## Dialogue

You can ask him why he joined:

:   **Why did you join the Dawnguard?**
:   *"I lost two wives to vampires. I will avenge them. It is good to know that I will not have to do it alone. I am glad this Dawnguard exists."*

When exiting conversation with him:

:   *"May your blades stay sharp."*

## Unused Scenes

In an earlier iteration of [A New Order](/wiki/Skyrim:A_New_Order "Skyrim:A New Order"), you were originally meant to start out at [Stendarr's Beacon](/wiki/Skyrim:Stendarr%27s_Beacon "Skyrim:Stendarr's Beacon"). Here, a meeting between [Isran](/wiki/Skyrim:Isran "Skyrim:Isran") and [Vigilant Tolan](/wiki/Skyrim:Vigilant_Tolan "Skyrim:Vigilant Tolan") would have taken place. At some unknown point after this, you would've been sent to Fort Dawnguard for the very first time, where you would've been greeted by this scene between Celann and Durak:

:   **Durak:** *"Here comes another one!"*
:   **Celann:** *"Hold it! She's/He's the one Tolan mentioned."*
:   **Durak:** *"Ugh. I thought this place was supposed to be secret?"*
:   **Celann:** *"Well it was... Thank the Vigilants for ruining that."*

## Notes

- Durak does not have a unique facial model, he instead uses the default male Orc face.
- Durak is the only add-on based Orc who you can recruit as a follower and the only one who can make you Blood-Kin.
- Durak's "No Crime" morality, combined with his high aggression value, may result in him attacking you if your bounty is high enough in The Rift.

Durian

Durian (also called **Dawnguard**) is an [Orc](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc "Skyrim:Orc") [Ranger](/wiki/Skyrim:Ranger_(class) "Skyrim:Ranger (class)") who can be found inside [Bloodchill Cavern](/wiki/Skyrim:Bloodchill_Cavern "Skyrim:Bloodchill Cavern"), attending the banquet during [Guests for Dinner](/wiki/Skyrim:Guests_for_Dinner "Skyrim:Guests for Dinner"). He's secretly a member of the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_(faction) "Skyrim:Dawnguard (faction)").

## Related Quests

- **[Guests for Dinner](/wiki/Skyrim:Guests_for_Dinner "Skyrim:Guests for Dinner")**[CC](/wiki/Skyrim:Bloodchill_Manor "Skyrim:Bloodchill Manor"): Attend a feast.

### Guests for Dinner

:   **Are you here for the dinner party?**
:   *"Yep."*

:   **Are all the guests present?**
:   *"It would seem so."*

After the vampires are killed (Player as a Non-Vampire):

:   **The vampires are all dead. And the will says the house belongs to me.**
:   *"Very good. But you've created a debt between us. Here. Take this. We are even now."*

He will then hand you the [Bloodchill Manor Key](/wiki/Skyrim:Bloodchill_Manor_Key "Skyrim:Bloodchill Manor Key").

## Notes

- He retains the changed name "Dawnguard" and can be found at [Candlehearth Hall](/wiki/Skyrim:Candlehearth_Hall "Skyrim:Candlehearth Hall") in [Windhelm](/wiki/Skyrim:Windhelm "Skyrim:Windhelm") after the completion of [Guests for Dinner](/wiki/Skyrim:Guests_for_Dinner "Skyrim:Guests for Dinner") as a Non-Vampire.
- Durian will not appear if you complete the quest [Guests for Dinner](/wiki/Skyrim:Guests_for_Dinner "Skyrim:Guests for Dinner") as a [Vampire](/wiki/Skyrim:Vampirism "Skyrim:Vampirism").

## Bugs

- Leaving the cavern before finishing the quest may cause Durian to be a permanent follower that is impossible to get rid of.

# Skyrim:Durnehviir (quest)

## Overview

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Learn a [dragon shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Shouts "Skyrim:Dragon Shouts") from [Durnehviir](/wiki/Skyrim:Durnehviir_(dragon) "Skyrim:Durnehviir (dragon)").** | |

| Reward: | [Summon Durnehviir](/wiki/Skyrim:Summon_Durnehviir "Skyrim:Summon Durnehviir") and [Soul Tear](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Tear "Skyrim:Soul Tear") shouts |
| ID: | DLC1VQDragon |
| --- | |
| |  |  | | --- | --- | | **← Previous** [Beyond Death](/wiki/Skyrim:Beyond_Death "Skyrim:Beyond Death") Can only be completed after [Dragon Rising](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Rising "Skyrim:Dragon Rising") |  | | |
| |  |  | | --- | --- | | ← Previous | [Beyond Death](/wiki/Skyrim:Beyond_Death "Skyrim:Beyond Death") Can only be completed after [Dragon Rising](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Rising "Skyrim:Dragon Rising") | | |

Summon [Durnehviir](/wiki/Skyrim:Durnehviir_(dragon) "Skyrim:Durnehviir (dragon)") to Tamriel!

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Spend three dragon souls to learn the words of [Durnehviir](/wiki/Skyrim:Durnehviir_(dragon) "Skyrim:Durnehviir (dragon)")'s shout.
2. [Summon Durnehviir](/wiki/Skyrim:Summon_Durnehviir "Skyrim:Summon Durnehviir") three times while outside of the [Soul Cairn](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Cairn "Skyrim:Soul Cairn") in order to learn [Soul Tear](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Tear "Skyrim:Soul Tear").

## Detailed Walkthrough

Durnehviir proclaims you Qahnaarin

After defeating him in the [Boneyard](/wiki/Skyrim:Boneyard "Skyrim:Boneyard"), [Durnehviir](/wiki/Skyrim:Durnehviir_(dragon) "Skyrim:Durnehviir (dragon)") will rematerialize outside, hailing you as his Qahnaarin. He will express his surprise and admiration of your fighting ability, stating that he has never been felled on the fields of the [Soul Cairn](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Cairn "Skyrim:Soul Cairn") before. He will then recount the tale of how he came to be bound into the service of the [Ideal Masters](/wiki/Lore:Ideal_Masters "Lore:Ideal Masters"), explaining that he was deceived after he sought their power to help establish his dominance among his fellow dovah on [Nirn](/wiki/Lore:Nirn "Lore:Nirn"). He will then teach you how to summon him back into Tamriel, promising to reward you each time you set him free.

Each time you do so, he will teach you another word of [Soul Tear](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Tear "Skyrim:Soul Tear"), a powerful [shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Shouts "Skyrim:Shouts") that deals a large amount of damage and doubles as a [Soul Trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Trap_(effect) "Skyrim:Soul Trap (effect)") and [Reanimate Corpse](/wiki/Skyrim:Reanimate_Corpse "Skyrim:Reanimate Corpse") spell. Moreover, after being summoned Durnehviir will also explain the meaning of each of those words. The first time he will be very glad to breathe Nirn's air once more: *"Ah! The free air of Vus at long last. As promised, I now teach you the first word of Soul Tearing: "Rii" - the essence of your enemy's life force."* As you summon him for the second time, he explains yet another word: *"I can feel my strength returning each time I am set free from that prison! Hear now the second word of Soul Tearing: "Vaaz" - meaning to tear your enemy's soul from its living vessel."* Unlike the Ideal Masters, this Dragon even after all the years of imprisonment, holds on to his honor and teaches you the third and final word of the Soul Tear shout, just as he promised: *"You have kept your side of the bargain, now let me fulfill mine. Feel the last word of Soul Tearing within yourself: "Zol" - the unlife that results when a soul is imprisoned in dead flesh."* Each word will require a Dragon Soul to learn, as if it had been learned from a [word wall](/wiki/Skyrim:Word_Wall "Skyrim:Word Wall").

## Notes

- You will need to activate all three words of the Summon Durnehviir shout in order to call him, which will require three Dragon Souls.
- Unlike the [Call Dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Call_Dragon "Skyrim:Call Dragon") shout, the Summon Durnehviir shout works like a Conjuration spell. You have to aim it at the ground and have enough space around the point of summoning for the shout to succeed. This also means that you can summon him within certain enclosed areas such as caves as long as there is enough room.

## Bugs

- You can learn the shout without being able to summon Durnehviir. This can happen if the game gives you all three words at once, and you leave for Tamriel without speaking to Durnehviir again before exiting the Soul Cairn.
  -  Use the console command `player.placeatme xx00C71A`. Kill the dragon that spawns, either using the console or otherwise. This will have to be done multiple times to get all the quests. You can also use console commands 'disable' and 'markfordelete' on each dragon.
- It is not necessary to summon Durnehviir to Tamriel. Summoning him in the Soul Cairn will have the same results and dialogue.
  -  The [Unofficial Dawnguard Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Dawnguard_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Dawnguard Patch"), version 1.1.4, fixes this bug.
- It is possible to kill Durnehviir when he appears a second time before he gets a chance to speak. The quest will then never initiate.
  - You can reset the quest and then set stage it to 30.
- It's possible that Durnehviir will disappear (be banished) shortly after summoning him, even not being able to finish his sentence regarding the Thu'um he is teaching. This, however won't prevent the acquisition of the word.
  - A possible solution seems to be pressing action (Activate; PC: "E") key pointing at Durnehviir while in the close proximity right after summoning him, as if one would like to interact with him. It will be entitled "<player\_name>'s Durnehviir", similar to how any other summoned creatures are described.
  - The partial solution is to quick save before summoning him and try - if he vanishes quick load and try summoning him some place else, even if it's only a few steps away.
- As Summon Durnehviir shout works like a Conjuration spell, it is subject to the same bugs (see [Conjuration bugs](/wiki/Skyrim:Conjuration#Bugs "Skyrim:Conjuration")). If you have a high [Spell Absorption](/wiki/Skyrim:Spell_Absorption "Skyrim:Spell Absorption") level (from the [Atronach Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Atronach_Stone "Skyrim:The Atronach Stone") and Atronach [Alteration perk](/wiki/Skyrim:Alteration#Skill_Perks "Skyrim:Alteration")), the shout will fail most of the time. One simple solution is to activate another stone, while learning the shout. **?**

## Quest Stages

| Stage | Finishes Quest | Journal Entry |

| 40 |  | *Objective 30:* Learn the second word of Durnehviir's Shout |
| 50 |  | *Objective 40:* Learn the final word of Durnehviir's Shout |
| 60 |  | I've now fully learned Durnehviir's shout by summoning him to Tamriel. Our agreement appears to be mutually beneficial, and therefore I'll continue to summon him as I deem necessary. |
| Durnehviir Misc Objective Handler (DLC1VQDragonMisc) | | |
| 10 |  | *Objective 10:* Speak to Durnehviir at his lair in the Soul Cairn |

- The following empty quest stages were omitted from the table:
  - DLC1VQDragon: 0, 10, 20, 35.
  - DLC1VQDragonMisc: 200.

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage DLC1VQDragon stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest DLC1VQDragon`.

Dushnamub

**Dushnamub** is an [Orc](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc "Skyrim:Orc") [warrior](/wiki/Skyrim:GuardOrc2H "Skyrim:GuardOrc2H") and resident [blacksmith](/wiki/Skyrim:Blacksmith "Skyrim:Blacksmith") for [Narzulbur](/wiki/Skyrim:Narzulbur "Skyrim:Narzulbur"), the [Orc stronghold](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc_Strongholds "Skyrim:Orc Strongholds") in [Eastmarch](/wiki/Skyrim:Eastmarch "Skyrim:Eastmarch"). He is the son of [Chief Mauhulakh](/wiki/Skyrim:Chief_Mauhulakh "Skyrim:Chief Mauhulakh"), and brother of [Urog](/wiki/Skyrim:Urog "Skyrim:Urog").

Dushnamub comes out of the [longhouse](/wiki/Skyrim:Mauhulakh%27s_Longhouse "Skyrim:Mauhulakh's Longhouse") around 8am and heads down to the forge to work. He doesn't offer any services until he is in place, and the walk can take him about an hour. At 8pm he heads back into the longhouse for dinner until going to sleep at midnight.

Dushnamub wears a set of [hide armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Hide_Armor "Skyrim:Hide Armor") with a matching pair of [boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Hide_Boots "Skyrim:Hide Boots"). He wields a leveled warhammer, which can be up to [Orcish](/wiki/Skyrim:Orcish "Skyrim:Orcish") in quality starting at level 6. He also carries a selection of [lower class loot and gold](/wiki/Skyrim:Leveled_Lists#Poor "Skyrim:Leveled Lists").

His mother died giving birth to him, and he was raised by his great-aunt, [Bolar](/wiki/Skyrim:Bolar "Skyrim:Bolar"). He is aware that his tribe is not common with Orcish tradition and will state so when approached.

In addition to his blacksmithing services, if you have any [ebony ore](/wiki/Skyrim:Ebony_Ore "Skyrim:Ebony Ore"), Dushnamub will purchase it from you.

## Related Quests

- **[Mine Ore](/wiki/Skyrim:Mine_Ore "Skyrim:Mine Ore")**: Get paid to [mine](/wiki/Skyrim:Mining "Skyrim:Mining") ore. ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))

## Dialogue

:   *"Haven't you seen how my aunts act with my father? It's beyond strange."*
:   *"I never knew my mother, but I doubt she ever acted as affectionate with my father as [Yatul](/wiki/Skyrim:Yatul "Skyrim:Yatul") and Bolar do."*
:   *"My sister is blind. I told her not to spend so much time with Yatul, but she won't listen. Thinks she's nice."*

### Conversations

Dushnamub can often be found confiding in his father:

:   **Dushnamub**: *"Don't you ever wonder, father?"*
:   **Mauhulakh**: *"All the time."*
:   **Dushnamub**: *"But your aunts don't even seem to care."*
:   **Mauhulakh**: *"They are good women. They love me. You will speak no more ill of them."*
:   **Dushnamub**: *"I've just never heard of a midwife losing all her mothers like that."*

:   **Dushnamub**: *"Father, I'm worried about Gadba and Mul."*
:   **Mauhulakh**: *"What about them?"*
:   **Dushnamub**: *"You don't worry about two Orc men coming into your stronghold? That they might challenge you?"*
:   **Mauhulakh**: *"They're miners. Harmless."*
:   **Dushnamub**: *"I've just learned not to trust luck around here."*

:   **Mauhulakh**: *"Someday, you can have your own stronghold."*
:   **Dushnamub**: *"I think it may have to be far away from here."*
:   **Mauhulakh**: *"Oh, if you're worried about me trying to meddle with you..."*
:   **Dushnamub**: *"It's not you I'm worried about."*

## Notes

- Dushnamub has two additional lines of dialogue which he was supposed to say after having completed [unfinished quest](/wiki/Skyrim:Unfinished_Quests "Skyrim:Unfinished Quests") `NarzulburFreeFormWifeQuest`, which involved getting an [unused NPC](/wiki/Skyrim:Uglarz "Skyrim:Uglarz") to return to Narzulbur in order to serve as Mauhulakh's new wife. He would speak positively of his father's new wife: *"Glad my father seems to have found someone. I just hope she can hold her own against my aunts."* and *"I think I like this new mate of my father's. I mean... nothing like that. I just think she's nice."*

## Bugs

- Dushnamub doesn't have the required keyword to pay for iron ore mined in Gloombound Mine if you try to sell them.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.9, fixes this bug.

## Overview

|  |  |  |

Dushnikh Mine

**Dushnikh Mine** is a small [orichalcum](/wiki/Skyrim:Orichalcum "Skyrim:Orichalcum") [mine](/wiki/Skyrim:Mines "Skyrim:Mines") supporting the [Orc stronghold](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc_Strongholds "Skyrim:Orc Strongholds") of [Dushnikh Yal](/wiki/Skyrim:Dushnikh_Yal "Skyrim:Dushnikh Yal"). It contains only one zone, *[Dushnikh Mine](#Dushnikh_Mine)*.

It is owned and worked by [Orcs](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc "Skyrim:Orc") from Dushnikh Yal. [Gharol](/wiki/Skyrim:Gharol "Skyrim:Gharol") will [buy orichalcum ore](/wiki/Skyrim:Mine_Ore "Skyrim:Mine Ore") from you.

## Residents*

| Residents |
| --- |
| [Dulug](/wiki/Skyrim:Dulug "Skyrim:Dulug")  [Ghak](/wiki/Skyrim:Ghak "Skyrim:Ghak")  [Mahk](/wiki/Skyrim:Mahk "Skyrim:Mahk")  [Oglub](/wiki/Skyrim:Oglub "Skyrim:Oglub") |

\* None of the miners ever seem to stop work for more than a few minutes or leave the mine even for sleep.

## Related Quests

- **[Mine Ore](/wiki/Skyrim:Mine_Ore "Skyrim:Mine Ore")**: Get paid to [mine](/wiki/Skyrim:Mining "Skyrim:Mining") ore. ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))

### Exterior

The exterior of the mine is the Orc stronghold of Dushnikh Yal. A [smelter](/wiki/Skyrim:Smelter "Skyrim:Smelter") is near the covered work area beneath the mine.

### Dushnikh Mine

There are numerous [pickaxes](/wiki/Skyrim:Pickaxe "Skyrim:Pickaxe") and [food](/wiki/Skyrim:Food "Skyrim:Food") sacks throughout the mine. Upon entering you are at the top of a ramp descending to the east, at the bottom is a cart containing five pieces of [orichalcum ore](/wiki/Skyrim:Orichalcum_Ore "Skyrim:Orichalcum Ore") (which are free to take if you are [blood-kin](/wiki/Skyrim:Blood-Kin "Skyrim:Blood-Kin") to the Orcs), with several food barrels behind. The path turns to the south, at the next junction there is a dead end to the east with a long wooden table and chair and an unlocked [chest](/wiki/Skyrim:Chest "Skyrim:Chest") containing minor loot. On the table is a copy of *[The Code of Malacath](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Code_of_Malacath "Skyrim:The Code of Malacath")*, a portion of [grilled leeks](/wiki/Skyrim:Grilled_Leeks "Skyrim:Grilled Leeks"), a [potion of minor healing](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Healing "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Healing"), a piece of orichalcum ore and a random pair of [gauntlets](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauntlets "Skyrim:Gauntlets"). To the west is another T-junction, with a rock pillar in front of you, on a rock behind it is a random [stamina](/wiki/Skyrim:Stamina "Skyrim:Stamina") [potion](/wiki/Skyrim:Potions "Skyrim:Potions") and [war axe](/wiki/Skyrim:War_Axe "Skyrim:War Axe"), to the north the path bears to the west with an orichalcum ore vein on the north wall and two [potions of minor stamina](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Stamina "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Stamina") (see [bugs](#Bugs)) on a rock almost opposite, against the south wall. Farther to the west are three more ore veins against the south wall and on the ground in front of it.

Heading south from the T-junction the path descends before turning to the east and opening out into a large cave with a raised wooden platform against the rear wall in front of you, the ramp up to it is on your right. There are two ore veins on the east wall reached by climbing the platform. At the end of the platform is a long wooden table and bench, with two bottles of [wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Wine "Skyrim:Wine") and a potion of minor healing on top the table. Under the platform against the east wall, on the ground is one final ore vein. In the northern corner of the lower area is a square wooden table with a loaf of [bread](/wiki/Skyrim:Bread "Skyrim:Bread") and mead barrel on top and a pair of [leather boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Leather_Boots "Skyrim:Leather Boots") next to two unusable barrels beside it.

## Bugs

- You may not be able to interact with the two potions of minor stamina found at the northern end of the mine.

## Maps

- 

  Dushnikh Mine

# Skyrim:Dushnikh Yal People

## Overview

|  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |

## Overview

Dushnikh Yal

**Dushnikh Yal** is a prosperous [Orc stronghold](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc_Strongholds "Skyrim:Orc Strongholds") in the southwest of [Skyrim](/wiki/Lore:Skyrim "Lore:Skyrim"), southeast of [Markarth](/wiki/Skyrim:Markarth "Skyrim:Markarth").

The stronghold contains three zones: *[Burguk's Longhouse](/wiki/Skyrim:Burguk%27s_Longhouse#Burguk.27s_Longhouse "Skyrim:Burguk's Longhouse")*, *[Burguk's Longhouse Cellar](/wiki/Skyrim:Burguk%27s_Longhouse#Burguk.27s_Longhouse_Cellar "Skyrim:Burguk's Longhouse")*, and *[Dushnikh Mine](/wiki/Skyrim:Dushnikh_Mine "Skyrim:Dushnikh Mine")*.

With the stronghold's hunters, [Arob](/wiki/Skyrim:Arob "Skyrim:Arob") and her son [Nagrub](/wiki/Skyrim:Nagrub "Skyrim:Nagrub"), providing [Hogni Red-Arm](/wiki/Skyrim:Hogni_Red-Arm "Skyrim:Hogni Red-Arm") with the meat that he sells in [Markarth's](/wiki/Skyrim:Markarth "Skyrim:Markarth") marketplace, and [Dushnikh Mine](/wiki/Skyrim:Dushnikh_Mine "Skyrim:Dushnikh Mine"), an [orichalcum](/wiki/Skyrim:Orichalcum "Skyrim:Orichalcum") mine containing seven [ore veins](/wiki/Skyrim:Orichalcum_Ore_Vein "Skyrim:Orichalcum Ore Vein"), the stronghold is thriving and fairly prosperous.

As with all [Orc strongholds](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc_Strongholds "Skyrim:Orc Strongholds"), you must become [Blood-Kin](/wiki/Skyrim:Blood-Kin "Skyrim:Blood-Kin") to the Orcs before you are welcome in the stronghold and able to barter or receive other services.

#### Miscellaneous Quests

- **[Fight! Fight!](/wiki/Skyrim:Fight!_Fight! "Skyrim:Fight! Fight!")**: Prove your strength by wagering on a fist fight with another. ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))
- **[Gharol's Message](/wiki/Skyrim:Gharol%27s_Message "Skyrim:Gharol's Message")**: Deliver [Gharol](/wiki/Skyrim:Gharol "Skyrim:Gharol")'s sword to [Lash](/wiki/Skyrim:Lash_gra-Dushnikh "Skyrim:Lash gra-Dushnikh").
- **[Mine Ore](/wiki/Skyrim:Mine_Ore "Skyrim:Mine Ore")**: Get paid to [mine](/wiki/Skyrim:Mining "Skyrim:Mining") ore. ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))
- **[The Forgemaster's Fingers](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Forgemaster%27s_Fingers "Skyrim:The Forgemaster's Fingers")**: Find [the Forgemaster's Fingers](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Forgemaster%27s_Fingers_(item) "Skyrim:The Forgemaster's Fingers (item)") to gain favor with the Orcs. ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))

## Walkthrough

It is a typical [Orc](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc "Skyrim:Orc") stronghold with a wooden palisade surrounding the longhouse and compound, with lookout platforms at regular intervals around the wall and a raised walkway around the inside of the wall. The longhouse is in the center of the compound with the separate activities arranged around it. There are two gates into the stronghold one to the east and the other to the west. On either side of the entrance to the longhouse is a covered seating area for [Chief Burguk](/wiki/Skyrim:Chief_Burguk "Skyrim:Chief Burguk") and a practice dummy used by [Ghorbash the Iron Hand](/wiki/Skyrim:Ghorbash_the_Iron_Hand "Skyrim:Ghorbash the Iron Hand") for up to twelve hours per day.

[Murbul](/wiki/Skyrim:Murbul "Skyrim:Murbul") spends her time working in an open-fronted hut at an [alchemy lab](/wiki/Skyrim:Alchemy_Lab "Skyrim:Alchemy Lab"). There is also a [tanning rack](/wiki/Skyrim:Tanning_Rack "Skyrim:Tanning Rack"), and set of shelves holding a random [magicka](/wiki/Skyrim:Magicka "Skyrim:Magicka") [potion](/wiki/Skyrim:Potions "Skyrim:Potions"), a random [healing](/wiki/Skyrim:Healing "Skyrim:Healing") potion, a bunch of [lavender](/wiki/Skyrim:Lavender "Skyrim:Lavender") and a [thistle branch](/wiki/Skyrim:Thistle_Branch "Skyrim:Thistle Branch") and three common books, including a copy of *[The Legend of Red Eagle](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Legend_of_Red_Eagle "Skyrim:The Legend of Red Eagle")*, which if you haven't already started the [quest](/wiki/Skyrim:Red_Eagle "Skyrim:Red Eagle") will initiate it. There are also a [garlic](/wiki/Skyrim:Garlic "Skyrim:Garlic") braid , two bunches of dried [elves ear](/wiki/Skyrim:Elves_Ear "Skyrim:Elves Ear") and a bunch of dried [frost mirriam](/wiki/Skyrim:Frost_Mirriam "Skyrim:Frost Mirriam") hanging from the roof and a drying frame. Farther to the northwest are two more huts that contain another tanning rack with a wooden table, shelves and a [food](/wiki/Skyrim:Food "Skyrim:Food") barrel. A [pheasant](/wiki/Skyrim:Pheasant "Skyrim:Pheasant") and [rabbit](/wiki/Skyrim:Rabbit_(dead) "Skyrim:Rabbit (dead)") are hanging from racks attached to the roof and several sacks of food respectively. Between these and the western gate is a pen for the [goat](/wiki/Skyrim:Goat "Skyrim:Goat"). South of the western gate are ramps passing a tree stump with a growth of [Mora Tapinella](/wiki/Skyrim:Mora_Tapinella "Skyrim:Mora Tapinella") fungi, leading up behind the longhouse to a decked area with a long wooden table and bench with three common books and a couple of flights of stairs leading up to a small [vegetable](/wiki/Skyrim:Food#Vegetables "Skyrim:Food") garden, with a couple of barrels, one of which contains [ingredients](/wiki/Skyrim:Ingredients "Skyrim:Ingredients").

South of the eastern gate is a ramp leading up to the blacksmithing area with a large open-fronted hut set behind a [forge](/wiki/Skyrim:Forge "Skyrim:Forge") where [Gharol](/wiki/Skyrim:Gharol "Skyrim:Gharol") and her son [Umurn](/wiki/Skyrim:Umurn "Skyrim:Umurn") spend their working day. The hut contains a [workbench](/wiki/Skyrim:Workbench "Skyrim:Workbench"), a [grindstone](/wiki/Skyrim:Grindstone "Skyrim:Grindstone"), a counter and long wooden table with an [iron warhammer](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Warhammer "Skyrim:Iron Warhammer"), a [steel greatsword](/wiki/Skyrim:Steel_Greatsword "Skyrim:Steel Greatsword"), an [iron shield](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Shield "Skyrim:Iron Shield"), a random [helmet](/wiki/Skyrim:Helmet "Skyrim:Helmet") and two [orichalcum ingot](/wiki/Skyrim:Orichalcum_Ingot "Skyrim:Orichalcum Ingot") on top. Just to the south is a [smelter](/wiki/Skyrim:Smelter "Skyrim:Smelter"). Which is next to another ramp, at the top of which is another tree stump with a mora tapinella fungus growing on it, past this is [Dushnikh mine](/wiki/Skyrim:Dushnikh_Mine "Skyrim:Dushnikh Mine"), an [orichalcum](/wiki/Skyrim:Orichalcum_Ore "Skyrim:Orichalcum Ore") mine.

| Crops | Mushrooms | Animals |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 9 [Cabbage](/wiki/Skyrim:Cabbage "Skyrim:Cabbage")  6 [Potato](/wiki/Skyrim:Potato "Skyrim:Potato") | 2 [Mora Tapinella](/wiki/Skyrim:Mora_Tapinella "Skyrim:Mora Tapinella") | 1 [Goat](/wiki/Skyrim:Goat "Skyrim:Goat") |

## Notes

- Internal names and unused dialogue for Chief Burguk show that the stronghold was originally known as **Shugurzbur**.
- In the DialogueViews files for the game, there exists a line (likely meant for the gate guard) that was meant to quickly establish the stronghold: *"This stronghold is Dushnikh Yal. Home of Burguk, chief of all Orcs in the Reach."*
- Asking [Hogni](/wiki/Skyrim:Hogni_Red-Arm "Skyrim:Hogni Red-Arm") about his meat will add a map marker for the stronghold to your map, if you have not yet discovered it on your own.

## Bugs

- Sometimes the alchemy lab in the longhouse basement is invisible. It still functions as an alchemy lab; it just cannot be seen.
- When accepting to brawl with Chief Burguk, the other members may fight you as if you have turned against them.

Duskglow Crevice

**Duskglow Crevice** is a small [cave](/wiki/Skyrim:Caves "Skyrim:Caves") south of [Dawnstar](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnstar "Skyrim:Dawnstar") containing [Falmer](/wiki/Skyrim:Falmer "Skyrim:Falmer"), [chaurus](/wiki/Skyrim:Chaurus "Skyrim:Chaurus"), [bandits](/wiki/Skyrim:Bandit "Skyrim:Bandit"), and [skeevers](/wiki/Skyrim:Skeever "Skyrim:Skeever"). It contains only one zone, *[Duskglow Crevice](#Duskglow_Crevice)*.

The Falmer and chaurus are battling a few remaining [bandits](/wiki/Skyrim:Bandit "Skyrim:Bandit"); you will encounter several bandit corpses as you explore.

## Related Quests

- This location is one of many potential targets for [one or more of the Radiant quests](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant#Quest_Locations "Skyrim:Radiant").

### Exterior

The main path leading to this cave is off of the road between Dawnstar and [Windhelm](/wiki/Skyrim:Windhelm "Skyrim:Windhelm"), not far north-northeast of the [Weynon Stones](/wiki/Skyrim:Weynon_Stones "Skyrim:Weynon Stones"). It is also possible to approach from [Fort Fellhammer](/wiki/Skyrim:Fort_Fellhammer "Skyrim:Fort Fellhammer"). In front of the entrance is an extinguished campfire, several [Falmer](/wiki/Skyrim:Falmer "Skyrim:Falmer") totems, and, immediately to the left, a patch of [bleeding crown](/wiki/Skyrim:Bleeding_Crown "Skyrim:Bleeding Crown") fungus.

### Duskglow Crevice

The entrance leads directly into a natural tunnel that descends to the north. As you follow the tunnel as it twists and turns, you may overhear and then encounter two bandits as they wander along the passage discussing the "cave people" who have been harassing and stealing from them. As you may have noticed from the chitinous decor, they are of course referring to the [Falmer](/wiki/Skyrim:Falmer "Skyrim:Falmer"). There are several patches of both bleeding crown and [fly amanita](/wiki/Skyrim:Fly_Amanita "Skyrim:Fly Amanita") fungi throughout the cave system. Just before you emerge onto a ravine ledge, there is also a patch of [white cap](/wiki/Skyrim:White_Cap "Skyrim:White Cap") fungus. Opposite is another ledge where two Falmer are battling a lone bandit. Once they have dealt with the bandit, if they have been alerted to your presence, they will immediately converge on you via a ledge they can drop down from the far side (see [notes](#Notes)). There is a gated passage at the back of the opposite ledge, while the one-way ledge is your shortcut back out later. It is possible using the [Whirlwind Sprint](/wiki/Skyrim:Whirlwind_Sprint "Skyrim:Whirlwind Sprint") [dragon shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Shouts "Skyrim:Dragon Shouts") or careful jumping to reach the far ledge; however, this is of little use, as there is no way of raising the gate blocking access to the remainder of the cave system from this side.

A path descends on your left, with several switchbacks before leading to a lower level that exits the ravine to the north. The passage is linear, and after a short distance it turns to the east and reaches a Falmer gate. Past the gate, the passage is filled with cobwebs, and you will encounter a couple skeevers. The passage continues to twist and turn, until you reach a point where the architecture changes to that typically found in Nord barrows. To your right is a throne, with a large [urn](/wiki/Skyrim:Urn "Skyrim:Urn") farther along to the right of a gap between two sections of Falmer fencing. Beyond this is a small Falmer encampment, with the path skirting around a small pool. Two Falmer inhabit the camp, one of which is leveled. There is nothing of interest in the water. The encampment consists of two Falmer tents. The tent to the north contains a small fire and has a loose [chaurus egg](/wiki/Skyrim:Chaurus_Eggs "Skyrim:Chaurus Eggs") in a wooden bowl and a [charred skeever hide](/wiki/Skyrim:Charred_Skeever_Hide "Skyrim:Charred Skeever Hide") on a flat rock in front. The tent to the southwest contains an unlocked Falmer [chest](/wiki/Skyrim:Chest "Skyrim:Chest"). There are two exits from this cave. The one to the northwest leads to a small cave containing a leveled [chaurus](/wiki/Skyrim:Chaurus "Skyrim:Chaurus"), many chaurus egg sacs, a [dead bandit](/wiki/Skyrim:Bandit_(dead) "Skyrim:Bandit (dead)"), and a [skeever tail](/wiki/Skyrim:Skeever_Tail "Skyrim:Skeever Tail") in a stone bowl under a decapitated skeever. The second exit is just to the right of the second tent.

The passage heads west then south, and opens into a cave with a leveled Falmer magic-user standing behind a flat-topped rock that's being used as an altar of sorts, with the body of a dead bandit in front beside a lit brazier and three loose chaurus eggs. On top of the rock is a [Falmer sword](/wiki/Skyrim:Falmer_Sword "Skyrim:Falmer Sword"), a random [poison](/wiki/Skyrim:Poisons "Skyrim:Poisons"), and a filled random [soul gem](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Gems "Skyrim:Soul Gems"). Behind the rock at the back of the cave is an unlocked Falmer chest, while the exit passage is found to the west. At the top, it turns south and enters a cave containing a leveled chaurus, with many more egg sacs around the cave and the body of yet another dead bandit. The exit is to the east and continues to climb. After a couple turns and just before it enters a room with more Nord barrow-style architecture, there is a [tripwire](/wiki/Skyrim:Tripwire "Skyrim:Tripwire") that triggers a [claw](/wiki/Skyrim:Claw "Skyrim:Claw") trap from above in front. On the right is a [burial urn](/wiki/Skyrim:Burial_Urn "Skyrim:Burial Urn"), while in front are wooden stairs leading up to a balcony with another burial urn at the far end and a doorway into a larger room where a leveled Falmer and leveled chaurus or [chaurus hunter](/wiki/Skyrim:Chaurus_Hunter "Skyrim:Chaurus Hunter")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") battle a bandit. This larger room is split into two levels. The lower level has more egg sacs, a broken cart with [tomatoes](/wiki/Skyrim:Tomato "Skyrim:Tomato") scattered across the floor, and opposite where you enter is the gated doorway seen near the beginning of the cave system. To the southwest is a sarcophagus with two burial urns beside it.

On the right, stone stairs rise to the upper level, where the fight took place. On the front edge, to the left, is a burning brazier with a chain beside it that opens the gate below. There are three sets of shelves against the south wall. The first holds a filled random soul gem, a random [potion](/wiki/Skyrim:Potions "Skyrim:Potions"), a random poison, and many [ruined books](/wiki/Skyrim:Ruined_Book "Skyrim:Ruined Book"). There is a food barrel to the right before the next shelves, which hold two [rock warbler eggs](/wiki/Skyrim:Rock_Warbler_Egg "Skyrim:Rock Warbler Egg"). The last set of shelves has a copy of *[Mixed Unit Tactics](/wiki/Skyrim:Mixed_Unit_Tactics "Skyrim:Mixed Unit Tactics")*, a pair of random [boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Armor#Boots "Skyrim:Armor"), two pieces of [firewood](/wiki/Skyrim:Firewood "Skyrim:Firewood"), and various cheap crockery and clutter. On top are a further four [common books](/wiki/Skyrim:Books "Skyrim:Books"). There is a stone table beside a partition near the stairs, with a [woodcutter's axe](/wiki/Skyrim:Woodcutter%27s_Axe "Skyrim:Woodcutter's Axe"), a copy of the [Pickpocket](/wiki/Skyrim:Pickpocket "Skyrim:Pickpocket") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[Purloined Shadows](/wiki/Skyrim:Purloined_Shadows "Skyrim:Purloined Shadows")*, a random [greatsword](/wiki/Skyrim:Greatsword "Skyrim:Greatsword") and [helmet](/wiki/Skyrim:Helmet "Skyrim:Helmet"), a chaurus egg, two bottles of [wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Wine "Skyrim:Wine"), a bottle of [Black-Briar Mead](/wiki/Skyrim:Black-Briar_Mead "Skyrim:Black-Briar Mead"), and a bowl of [ectoplasm](/wiki/Skyrim:Ectoplasm "Skyrim:Ectoplasm") on top. Some of the items may have been knocked off the table during the fight. Beside the table is a stone bowl on the ground containing four [leeks](/wiki/Skyrim:Leek "Skyrim:Leek"), and beside this is a basket containing two bunches of [lavender](/wiki/Skyrim:Lavender "Skyrim:Lavender").

In the final chamber, a chain near a brazier on the upper level opens the gate below, providing the quickest exit.

Against the north wall are two sets of shelves. The first holds a piece of firewood, a [cow hide](/wiki/Skyrim:Cow_Hide "Skyrim:Cow Hide"), and a [corundum ingot](/wiki/Skyrim:Corundum_Ingot "Skyrim:Corundum Ingot"), with a [horse hide](/wiki/Skyrim:Horse_Hide "Skyrim:Horse Hide") on the floor in front (see [bugs](#Bugs)) and a [lute](/wiki/Skyrim:Lute "Skyrim:Lute") leaning against the side. The second holds a random helmet and another lute. In the middle of the room is a campfire with a [cooking pot](/wiki/Skyrim:Cooking_Pot "Skyrim:Cooking Pot") on a stand beside it, and by a stone pillar is a rack hanging from the ceiling holding a [garlic braid](/wiki/Skyrim:Garlic_Braid "Skyrim:Garlic Braid") and [pheasant](/wiki/Skyrim:Pheasant "Skyrim:Pheasant"). Beside another pillar is an end table with a [moth in a jar](/wiki/Skyrim:Moth_in_a_Jar "Skyrim:Moth in a Jar") on top. Toward the rear of the room are several strings of [bone chimes](/wiki/Skyrim:Bone_Chimes "Skyrim:Bone Chimes") hanging from the ceiling. Against the west wall is an upright sarcophagus with a small, medium, and large [coin purse](/wiki/Skyrim:Coin_Purse "Skyrim:Coin Purse") to the right, and farther to the right, on the ground is a bottle of Black-Briar Mead. To the left is a stone table with an unlocked Falmer chest, a copy of the [Lockpicking](/wiki/Skyrim:Lockpicking "Skyrim:Lockpicking") skill book *[The Wolf Queen, v1](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Wolf_Queen,_v1 "Skyrim:The Wolf Queen, v1")*, a common book, a [ruby](/wiki/Skyrim:Ruby "Skyrim:Ruby"), and a [flute](/wiki/Skyrim:Flute "Skyrim:Flute") on top.

Passing through the gate will bring you back to the ledge near the entrance upon which you saw the battle between two Falmer and a bandit, overlooking the ravine. Follow the ledge on the left to drop down and retrace your steps for a quick exit.

## Notes

- It is entirely possible for the two Falmer to cross the ravine before you enter and attack the two bandits waiting in the entrance passage. If this has happened, and they have killed the two bandits before you arrive, they may be lying in wait anywhere, and may even have gone down into the bottom of the ravine. Also, if they have crossed the ravine, the chaurus hunter in the final cave (across the ravine behind the barred gate) may show on your compass bar as a hostile, even though it is behind the gate.
- In [Survival Mode](/wiki/Skyrim:Survival_Mode "Skyrim:Survival Mode"), this dungeon will not warm you up, unlike most interior locations.

## Bugs

- You may not be able to interact with the horse hide and with one of the rock warbler eggs.

## Maps

- 

  Duskglow Crevice

# Skyrim:Dustman's Cairn

## Overview

Dustman's Cairn

**Dustman's Cairn** is a medium-sized [Nordic ruin](/wiki/Skyrim:Nordic_Ruins "Skyrim:Nordic Ruins") northwest of [Whiterun](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun "Skyrim:Whiterun") containing [Silver Hands](/wiki/Skyrim:Silver_Hand "Skyrim:Silver Hand"), [draugr](/wiki/Skyrim:Draugr "Skyrim:Draugr"), [frostbite spiders](/wiki/Skyrim:Frostbite_Spider "Skyrim:Frostbite Spider"), and [skeevers](/wiki/Skyrim:Skeever "Skyrim:Skeever"). It contains two zones: *[Dustman's Cairn](#Dustman.27s_Cairn)* and *[Dustman's Crypt](#Dustman.27s_Crypt)*.

Its [word wall](/wiki/Skyrim:Word_Wall "Skyrim:Word Wall") teaches part of the [Fire Breath](/wiki/Skyrim:Fire_Breath "Skyrim:Fire Breath") [dragon shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Shouts "Skyrim:Dragon Shouts"). Before the quest [Proving Honor](/wiki/Skyrim:Proving_Honor "Skyrim:Proving Honor"), most of the ruin will be inaccessible.

## Related Quests

- **[Proving Honor](/wiki/Skyrim:Proving_Honor "Skyrim:Proving Honor")**: Claim a [Fragment of Wuuthrad](/wiki/Skyrim:Fragment_of_Wuuthrad "Skyrim:Fragment of Wuuthrad") from Dustman's Cairn.

- This location is one of many potential targets for [one or more of the Radiant quests](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant#Quest_Locations "Skyrim:Radiant").

### Exterior

There is little of value outside the cairn. Many flowers typical of the central tundra of [Whiterun Hold](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun_Hold "Skyrim:Whiterun Hold") grow outside the entrance, including [lavender](/wiki/Skyrim:Lavender "Skyrim:Lavender"), [mountain flowers](/wiki/Skyrim:Blue_Mountain_Flower "Skyrim:Blue Mountain Flower"), and [tundra cotton](/wiki/Skyrim:Tundra_Cotton "Skyrim:Tundra Cotton"), and eleven [hanging moss](/wiki/Skyrim:Hanging_Moss "Skyrim:Hanging Moss") and an [iron shield](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Shield "Skyrim:Iron Shield") are found inside the structure.

A well-maintained road runs between [Hamvir's Rest](/wiki/Skyrim:Hamvir%27s_Rest "Skyrim:Hamvir's Rest") nearby to the north and [Fort Greymoor](/wiki/Skyrim:Fort_Greymoor "Skyrim:Fort Greymoor") to the south, with a short dirt path leading north to Dustman's Cairn. An upturned cart with a scattered cargo of [cabbages](/wiki/Skyrim:Cabbage "Skyrim:Cabbage") is near the intersection of the road and path.

### Dustman's Cairn

A draugr welcoming party

You enter at the top of a short set of stairs. When you descend the steps, if you are not on the quest Proving Honor, three draugr emerge from upright sarcophagi on either side of the room and attack. If you are there as part of the quest, Farkas will be accompanying you. The three [dead draugr](/wiki/Skyrim:Containers#Draugr "Skyrim:Containers") will be lying near the three sarcophagi. Regardless, check the table in the middle of the room for a copy of the [Two-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:Two-handed "Skyrim:Two-handed") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[Battle of Sancre Tor](/wiki/Skyrim:Battle_of_Sancre_Tor "Skyrim:Battle of Sancre Tor")*. Beside the book is a [pickaxe](/wiki/Skyrim:Pickaxe "Skyrim:Pickaxe") and a [lockpick](/wiki/Skyrim:Lockpick "Skyrim:Lockpick"). There is also a novice-locked chest beside the table. Two sideboards flank the stairs leading down from the entrance, one with some clutter, the other with a pickaxe and a bowl of [bone meal](/wiki/Skyrim:Bone_Meal "Skyrim:Bone Meal") on top. Around the room are two [bleeding crown](/wiki/Skyrim:Bleeding_Crown "Skyrim:Bleeding Crown") fungus, and two hanging moss. The path forward is opposite the entrance, it will be blocked by fallen rocks before the quest is started. Among the rubble to the right of the passage is another pickaxe, and as you continue there are numerous hanging moss and various fungi throughout the ruins, some of the moss is unreachable.

The next area contains four draugr, all of whom are standing in alcoves, in wait for unwary explorers. The first room to the right contains one of these draugr and a bleeding crown fungus. The room with the lantern contains another draugr. The third draugr is in the room opposite, in an alcove on the front left-hand side. The final draugr is wandering to the left as you follow the path northward to the next section of the dungeon.

The throne room

Through the door is a tunnel is covered with a thin cobweb you can walk through; on the floor, to the right is an [orange dartwing](/wiki/Skyrim:Orange_Dartwing "Skyrim:Orange Dartwing"). At the other end of the tunnel is a broken table and two dead draugr on the floor, beside one of these is an [ancient Nord war axe](/wiki/Skyrim:Ancient_Nord_War_Axe "Skyrim:Ancient Nord War Axe"). There are two [iron ingots](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Ingot "Skyrim:Iron Ingot") on shelves to the left of the table. The next room is safe to enter. To the left, down the stairs, are two thrones and an [arcane enchanter](/wiki/Skyrim:Arcane_Enchanter "Skyrim:Arcane Enchanter"). Across the room, on a set of shelves, is a random [potion of the berserker](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_the_Berserker "Skyrim:Potion of the Berserker") and a [leather strip](/wiki/Skyrim:Leather_Strips "Skyrim:Leather Strips"). There is another set of shelves on the other side of the room holding a random [potion of the defender](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_the_Defender "Skyrim:Potion of the Defender") and a goat hide. Against the south wall is a stone table with a dead draugr on top. The path forward, to the southeast, is blocked; you will need to activate a lever in the room to the northeast. The room with the lever also contains a bowl of bone meal, a [potion of minor stamina](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Stamina "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Stamina"), a [potion of minor healing](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Healing "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Healing"), a leather strip and a leveled healing potion.

Follow the twisting path until you turn east. You will then see two Silver Hands conversing on the other side of a raised section of the tunnel. When they are dead, check the first alcove on the right for a random [helmet](/wiki/Skyrim:Helmet "Skyrim:Helmet") on a plinth that is [trapped](/wiki/Skyrim:Weight_Sensitive_Plate "Skyrim:Weight Sensitive Plate") and triggers a [dart trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Dart_Trap "Skyrim:Dart Trap") from the north. There is a second orange dartwing on the ground. On the pedestal in the second alcove is a [flawless amethyst](/wiki/Skyrim:Flawless_Amethyst "Skyrim:Flawless Amethyst") and some loose [septims](/wiki/Skyrim:Gold "Skyrim:Gold"). There is an [imp stool](/wiki/Skyrim:Imp_Stool "Skyrim:Imp Stool") fungus beside the pedestal, and a bowl of bone meal on some shelves beside where the Silver Hands stood. The only items of interest in the next room are a pickaxe near a gap through which you can see deeper into the ruins and a [luna moth wing](/wiki/Skyrim:Luna_Moth_Wing "Skyrim:Luna Moth Wing") on the left by some cobwebs (as well as a [blue dartwing](/wiki/Skyrim:Blue_Dartwing "Skyrim:Blue Dartwing") hidden behind the basket).

Through the next door, are more catacombs with a draugr lying in wait; it is in an alcove opposite the door and slightly to the right. There is also an [urn](/wiki/Skyrim:Urn "Skyrim:Urn") and two dead draugr that can be looted. The next room is to the east and contains a Silver Hand standing over a bloodstained draugr and another Silver Hand patrolling the walkways above the far side of the room. There is a novice-locked chest under the stairs and a small [coin purse](/wiki/Skyrim:Coin_Purse "Skyrim:Coin Purse") on the ground in the eastern corner. Ascend the stairs and turn around to the left. Search for a chain hanging from the wall beyond the rubble. This lowers a secret area to the left of the stairs that contains a high-leveled chest. There is a [dead Silver Hand warrior](/wiki/Skyrim:Silver_Hand_Warrior "Skyrim:Silver Hand Warrior") lying on one of the sarcophagi and a level draugr to deal with. There are several urns and [burial urns](/wiki/Skyrim:Burial_Urn "Skyrim:Burial Urn") in this area and through the door to the east, a master-locked chest and behind the left-hand door, a large coin purse. Before descending the stairs to the south, grab the [pine thrush egg](/wiki/Skyrim:Pine_Thrush_Egg "Skyrim:Pine Thrush Egg"), [silver amethyst ring](/wiki/Skyrim:Silver_Amethyst_Ring "Skyrim:Silver Amethyst Ring") and hanging moss near the brazier to the left. On a table to the right of the stairs is a random [sword](/wiki/Skyrim:Sword "Skyrim:Sword"), eleven loose septims, two [potions of minor magicka](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Magicka "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Magicka"), and two potions of minor healing. Beside the table is a burial urn, with another two on ledges above; one of these you will have to jump to reach as it is to the south, on top of the wall separating this area with the previous area where the pickaxe and luna moth wing were found.

There are more draugr in the next section. The first is again lying in wait in front and slightly to the right of the door. There is one around the corner to the right by a large urn, and another to the left of some rubble farther along the path. There is another draugr in an alcove to the left, another on the left by the rubble with two large urns among it, and one more straight ahead. There is a Silver Hand patrolling around here too. Past the Silver Hand and a broken urn is the final living draugr. Near the top of a slope there is an [ancient Nord battle axe](/wiki/Skyrim:Ancient_Nord_Battle_Axe "Skyrim:Ancient Nord Battle Axe") lying on the ground, with a second one among the rubble on the right. Down the slope is a dead draugr by an adept-locked chest, with two burial urns to the left in an upper alcove. To the south is a flight of stair with a wooden door at the bottom. On the right is an urn and burial urn.

The next room is populated by more Silver Hands. The first stands lookout on the platform straight ahead on the far side of the room, and to the upper right. There are [white cap](/wiki/Skyrim:White_Cap "Skyrim:White Cap") fungi in the northeast and southwest corners of the first area. There are two Silver Hands standing by the fire in the middle of the second part of the room. The ramp to the first Silver Hand is here, going back past you. Through the next door, behind the door to the left is a medium coin purse along with two rings (on the hand of a skeleton poking through some rubble and roots), and partway down in the middle of the stairs, is a [pressure plate](/wiki/Skyrim:Pressure_Plate "Skyrim:Pressure Plate") that triggers a poison dart trap from the right-hand wall. Two Silver Hands are at the bottom, hiding behind the pillars one on either side. There is an unlocked chest to the far left of corner before the final door.

### Dustman's Crypt

Silver Hands fighting draugr

There is a Silver Hand leaning on a sarcophagus around a corner when you enter the crypt (on the right just before the wooden door in front). Through the door is an enclosed walkway above a large room: there are two Silver Hands below, who may provoke some of the draugr in the room. It is also possible to snipe the combatants with ranged attacks. More draugr lie in wait along the next corridor. The first is around the corner in the first alcove, the following two are on the outside of the corner (there is also a white cap fungus here). Down the slope is another white cap fungus, with a draugr on either side of the tunnel. Around the corner from here is a Silver Hand, and two draugr lying in alcoves on the left-hand wall: these two will usually have been awakened by the presence of the Silver Hand. There is a final draugr in an alcove opposite the rubble up ahead. There is a white cap fungus lying loose at the corner and another two more loose fungi in the rubble farther along and also one growing and an urn with some loot right at the top of the rubble. There is a chest in an alcove to the right.

The corridor eventually ends above a room with a Silver Hand; once dealt with, loot the [apothecary's satchel](/wiki/Skyrim:Apothecary%27s_Satchel "Skyrim:Apothecary's Satchel") found on the sideboard to the right of the entrance. Underneath the stairs is an adept-locked chest. There are five burial urns spread around the preparation table opposite the chest. Opening the adept-locked door to the south reveals a selection of rare [ingredients](/wiki/Skyrim:Ingredients "Skyrim:Ingredients"): there is a bowl of [vampire dust](/wiki/Skyrim:Vampire_Dust "Skyrim:Vampire Dust"), [frost salts](/wiki/Skyrim:Frost_Salts "Skyrim:Frost Salts"), two bowls of bone meal, a sample of [ice wraith teeth](/wiki/Skyrim:Ice_Wraith_Teeth "Skyrim:Ice Wraith Teeth") and a [potion of cure disease](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Cure_Disease "Skyrim:Potion of Cure Disease").

The next room is the one seen from the previous walkway. There is a chest to the left that contains the [Dustman's Cairn key](/wiki/Skyrim:Dustman%27s_Cairn_Key "Skyrim:Dustman's Cairn Key") among its loot. The key is needed for the far door, which is key-locked. There are two burial urns on the left and on a sideboard by a stone pillar near the middle of the room is a steel ingot and a stone bowl containing a leather strip. There is nothing else of interest except for any remaining enemies that you will have taken care of at this point. Beyond the locked door is a wide passage guarded by several skeevers. It ends with a door leading to a room that contains an [alchemy lab](/wiki/Skyrim:Alchemy_Lab "Skyrim:Alchemy Lab") and a table with three dead draugr lying on top. There is a novice-locked door to the southwest, behind which is an urn and a potion of minor healing. To the west is a cave-in with another burial urn among the rubble and a door opposite to the east.

A well-preserved carving with a valuable gem

Through the door to the east is the tunnel that allows you to continue; there is also another skeever there. There is another skeever in the tunnel, and two frostbite spiders when the tunnel opens out, as well as an [egg sac](/wiki/Skyrim:Egg_Sac "Skyrim:Egg Sac") to the right and a couple of desiccated corpses that can be looted. You will need to take the higher path around the sides of the cave to progress, as the lower path is a dead end, and too high to jump up. There are two leveled draugr, one of which is a magic-user between the second bridge and the exit to the cave. In the corridor after this, there is a carving on the wall to the right, with a bright [ruby](/wiki/Skyrim:Ruby "Skyrim:Ruby") lodged in the middle carving. The corridor after this contains only a white cap fungus, a hanging moss (both mid-way through the corridor), and some dead draugr.

The word wall

Through the iron door is the final room of the dungeon, which contains a word wall for the Fire Breath shout, a [fragment of Wuuthrad](/wiki/Skyrim:Fragment_of_Wuuthrad "Skyrim:Fragment of Wuuthrad"), and many draugr. The draugr will only be activated once the fragment is taken. This also means that the shortcut back to the entrance of the cairn is inaccessible, as it is through a sarcophagus atop the stairs. There are a total of seventeen draugr that come alive, including a boss-leveled one. Additionally, the iron door magically locks with an apprentice lock. This door doesn't unlock after the battle. Beside the fragment are two random healing potions and three random [soul gems](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Gems "Skyrim:Soul Gems") (all the way up to [black](/wiki/Skyrim:Black_Soul_Gem "Skyrim:Black Soul Gem")). There is a boss chest to the right of the word wall, and a few urns by the stairs to the right. The exit tunnel leads to the northwesterly sarcophagi in the very first room. Don't forget to pull the lever to lower the hidden wall.

## Notes

- Unless you are on the quest Proving Honor, you will only have access to the first room, which is guarded by three leveled draugr.
- It is possible to use a rune spell to activate the draugr in the final room in smaller numbers prior to taking the fragment. This makes the final battle easier.
- If you have been sent here by a radiant quest after completing the quest Proving Honor, you will need to reload your game and ask the quest giver for another radiant quest. This is because this location does not respawn, and you will be unable to complete the quest. If you have received the radiant quest before starting Proving Honor, you should still be able to complete it while concurrently completing Proving Honor.
- If you do not want to join the Companions but still want the word for the Fire Breath shout, you can glitch through the door fronted by loose pottery by holding a wooden plate against it then running against the plate or using the [Whirlwind Sprint](/wiki/Skyrim:Whirlwind_Sprint "Skyrim:Whirlwind Sprint") shout until you clip through the door, then proceed down the tunnel. The back of a leveled draugr will be before you; if you kill it in one strike, the coffin lid will fall, allowing you access to the rest of the ruin, and if not, you will have to pass through it using the wooden plate glitch. It is advised not to take the fragment of Wuuthrad on the table, as it will persist in your inventory as a quest item. The word wall will still teach the word if you enter this way, and the boss chest will still contain loot. You can even explore the rest of the ruin by using the wooden plate glitch to pass through any key-locked doors, and the hostile Silver Hands will still be present.

## Bugs

- Although geographically located in [Whiterun Hold](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun_Hold "Skyrim:Whiterun Hold"), Dustman's Cairn is erroneously marked as being in [the Reach](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Reach "Skyrim:The Reach"). This means that [radiant quests](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant_Quests "Skyrim:Radiant Quests") which would otherwise be confined to the Reach may send you here instead.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.1.1, fixes this bug.

## Maps

- 

  Dustman's Cairn
- 

  Dustman's Crypt
